207                            ANNEX 6
KYRGYZ REPUBLIC
HEALTH SECTOR REFORM PROJECT
ANNEX 6: PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION AND MANAGEMENT ARRANGEMENTS
A. Project Implementation
1.    The overall implementation and administration of the project would be the responsibility of the
Ministry of Health. To assist in the various aspects of the project, the MOH would depend upon several
entities to provide policy advice, technical direction and specialized services. These would be carried
out, respectively, by a Project Policy Council (PPC), a Technical Coordination Committee (TCC), and
the Project Coordination Unit (PCU) of the Social Safety Net project.
B. The Role of the Project Policy Council
2.    The Project Policy Council would oversee the policies undertaken by the MOH and other entities
involved in project implementation to reform the health sector. It is chaired by the Minister of Health
or his designee, and members would include MOH Deputy Ministers, representatives from the involved
departments of the MOH, Chui and Issyk-Kul oblasts and Bishkek city medical officials, Pharmacia,
representatives from the medical community and a representative from the Ministry of Finance. It would
advise the Minister on all important policy aspects of the project and would meet once every three
months, or more often if its Chairman so decides. The Technical Coordination Committee (TCC) would
serve as the secretariat of the Project Policy Council. The TCC Director would prepare minutes of the
PC meetings and ensure that the decisions taken by the PC are implemented by the implementing
agencies/entities.
3.    The Project Policy Council has the responsibility to ensure that the objectives of the Project are
fulfilled. Among its major tasks, are:
(i)    To review the periodic project implementation reports prepared by the TCC and the
quarterly implementation schedules. Discuss any problems or issues resulting in delays
and approve necessary actions to be taken to solve problems in project implementation.
(ii)   To discuss and resolve issues linked to project implementation that cannot be resolved
by the implementing agencies/entities and the TCC and decide, in consultation with the
Bank, on all policy issues linked to project implementation.
(iii)   To facilitate coordination with other projects and activities relevant to the reform of the
health sector, and coordinate policy issues with the Donor Community in the country.
C. The Role of the Technical Coordination Committee
4.    The Technical Coordination Committee (TCC) would manage the technical implementation of the
project. It is headed by a Director who reports to the designated Deputy Minister of Health, who serves
as the Ministry's counterpart and chief liaison officer with the Bank for the project, on a day-to-day basis.
It is comprised of a full-time Director and four technical advisors acceptable to the Bank who would
be designated as Component Coordinators (CC). The Director has a relevant degree and experience in
the health sector. The Director and technical staff are assisted by an administrative assistant. The TCC
would function on a permanent basis. In addition, current operating personnel from each organization
who are assigned to implement a specific activity (e.g. tuberculosis, drug regulatory organization, etz.)



208                                 ANNEX 6
within each of the four components would be named as a liaison person to the TCC, and would be
responsible for the day-to-day management of their respective activities.
5.     The TCC would provide the technical direction to the several components and sub-components.
It would formulate and recommend for approval any policy reforms associated with the project, and
periodically assess the status of and progress towards overall project goals. It would coordinate activities
among the components, and also coordinate the project's activities with the other donor activities in the
health sector. It would coordinate the budget planning and control of project funds, and coordinate with
the Ministry of Finance as required. Problems which are not resolved at the component level would be
raised to the TCC.  The TCC  would request and authorize the PCU  to prepare disbursement
documentation for signature by the Minister or his designee for payment of goods and services. Finally,
the TCC would maintain progress indicators, design and arrange for periodic project evaluations and
manage the periodic meetings of the PC. The MOH provides adequate office space, local telephone
service, local transportation expenses, an administrative assistant and two positions seconded to the PCU
which would be funded through MOH budgetary resources. The project would finance specialized
technical services, the TCC Director, the four TCC technical component coordinators, international
communications, office equipment and one vehicle.''
6.     The following specific functions would be performed by the TCC under the direction of the
Director:
(i)    Comply with directives of the Project Council and coordination of all activities needed
for project execution.
(ii)    Prepare guidelines for planning, preparation, supervision, administration and execution
of project activities in accordance with the agreements to be agreed upon by the Bank and
the Government in the proposed Loan Agreement.
(iii)    Provide the technical, and in cooperation with the PCU, administrative and logistical
assistance necessary for the implementing entities under the project.
(iv)    Establish working relationships with the Director of the PCU and reach agreement upon
a master procurement plan.
(v)    Monitor project progress, coordinate all project activities among components and assist
in the coordination between the MOH, MOF, Oblast and Municipal Governments, the
medical community and other donors to assure a consistent approach in project
implementation.
(vi)    With the participation of the CCs, prepare and maintain a Project Master Implementation
Plan, which would include Component Detailed Implementation Plans.
(vii)   Prepare and maintain a consolidated project budget for the project and maintain liaison
with the Ministry of Finance on project financial and budget issues.
11/ lhe Director and four technical advisors would serve as local consultants and receive compensation comparable to that now paid to local
consultants under the Manas project (i.e. not to exceed tde equivalent US$200 per month for the Director and $150 per month for each of the
component coordinators). Their appointment would be on a year-to-year basis subject to renewal based upon performance and fulfillmeut of
project goals.



209                             ANNEX 6
(viii)  Prepare and approve all terms of reference for consultants who would assist in
implementation of the project. Ensure that technical assistance being provided meets
these objectives.
(ix)   Design and implement evaluation of project components and overall policy objectives.
(x)    Serve as the secretariat to the Project Council and prepare all meetings, maintain minutes
and follow-up on all recommendations and actions.
(xi)   Ensure that all necessary technical reports and records are maintained, and that annual
audits are performed.
(xii)   Maintain records of project progress indicators for each activity.
(xiii)  On the advice of the CCs, authorize the PCU to prepare Withdrawal Applications to be
signed by the Minister or his designee and sent to the Bank for payment for goods and
services financed from the project.
D. The Role of Component Coordinators
7.    The Director of the TCC would be assisted by four technical advisors who would proved policy
and technical direction to the four functional sectors of activity under the project, namely (i) primary
health care, (ii) facilities management, (iii) medical care provider payments, and (iv) pharmaceutical
management. Their responsibility is to ensure that the day-to-day managers, i.e. the individuals within
each activity who are assigned the responsibility of implementing their specific activity, receive the
necessary support and policy guidance to execute their activities, and also to ensure that the separate
activities are coordinated within the overall program of reform. This includes the coordination with other
donor activities, and the sharing of information and problem solving among all the participating agencies
and entities. They would be responsible for preparing training plans and arranging for their execution
within their respective sector. They would be responsible to report to the TCC Director all significant
activities, progress, problems or policy issues which emerge in their sector, and make recommendations
for action. They would follow up on all relevant recommendations of the Project Policy Council, and
prepare or cause to be prepared any reports required in the execution of the activities within their sector.
8.    The implementation of each component would be monitored and coordinated by each TCC
Component Coordinator (CC) who would work closely with the individuals in the MOH and within the
health sector in each activity who are in charge of the day-to-day implementation of specific activities.
The CCs would report directly to the Director of the TCC, and the lead individuals in each activity would
report to the head of their respective organization or department, but would cooperate closely with the
respective technical advisor in the TCC overseeing the implementation of their activity. The CC is
responsible for the following tasks:
(i)    Ensure coordination of the activates undertaken by the various agencies or departments
within their component or activity. Ensure that each unit of the entity has a clear
understanding of its role and responsibilities under tte project.
(ii)   Ensure the effective and efficient implementation of the component and that the project
implementation schedule is respected. Inform the head of the implementing entity and
the TCC of any slippage in implementation and propose actions to correct the problems.



210                            ANNEX 6
(iii)   Bring any issues of policy or donor coordination relevant to the implementation of the
activity to the attention of the Head of the implementing department and the TCC.
(iv)   Prepare, in cooperation with relevant units of the implementing entity and the PCU, lists
and specifications of equipment to be purchased under the project and terms of reference
(TOR) for required technical assistance.
(v)    Participate in the evaluation process of awards of procurement actions organized by the
PCU.
(vi)   Advise the TCC of the successful delivery of goods and services provided under the
project and recommend to the TCC that payment be authorized.
(vii)  Prepare regular implementation reports on component implementation for submission to
the TCC. Update quarterly implementation schedules. Hold frequent meetings with the
TCC to discuss implementation issues.
E. The Role of the Project Coordination Unit
9.    The PCU of the Social Safety Net project would serve as the procurement and administrative
"agent" of the MOH for the Health Sector Reform project. As such it would be a project implementation
unit servicing the specific needs of the project in those administrative functions required for efficient
project management and implementation. The MOH and the PCU have signed an agreement outlining
their respective roles and responsibilities, and the costs thereof to the PCU to be financed by the MOH
under the project as "consultant services". The MOH provides the PCU with two staff members of the
MOH to be trained by the PCU during the execution of the project, and at the end of the project they
would return to the MOH and serve as a nucleus for the MOH to establish a procurement office in the
future. The Project, under "consultant services", would finance the direct costs and services of the PCU
related to the Health Sector Reform project only, general and specialized procurement specialists in
pharmaceuticals, medical equipment, and civil works administration. Specifically, the PCU would
perform the following functions:
(i)    Procurement: provide assistance, advice, and contract management to the implementing
departments and entities in the procurement of civil works, equipment, pharmaceuticals
and related services. It would also provide assistance, advice and contract management
in the recruitment of consultants and technical assistance/training services. The PCU
would prepare all tender documents and technical specifications, and manage the process
of receiving and evaluating competitive proposals (with the active participation of the
TCC and CCs).
(ii)   Finance and Accounting: prepare and maintain project detailed and summary accounting
and financial analysis records and reports. It would also arrange for and execute all
necessary project account audits.
(iii)   Disbursements: acting on the advice of the TCC and the CCs, prepare and process Bank
Withdrawal Applications and disbursements of project funds, and maintain all necessary
special accounts of project funds.



211                              ANNEX 6
(iv)   Reporting: prepare all necessary reports required by the Bank. For technical and
periodic quarterly progress reports, the PCU would insure that the TCC and CCs prepare
their contributions in a timely manner.
(v)    Civil Works: prepare bidding documents and contracts acceptable to the Bank for the
rehabilitation activities in the two Oblasts included under the project. Design and
implement a system of supervision involving the local community, MOH on-site
personnel and independent engineers.
(vi)   Bank Guidelines: Ensure that all procurement actions meet Bank Guidelines and that
Bank no objections are sought and obtained as necessary.
F. Specific Terms of Reference for Project Administration Staff
The Director of the Technical Coordination Committee
10.   The Director of the TCC would have responsibility for the following tasks:
(i)    Provide leadership for the overall technical direction and implementation of the Project.
This would include managing the administration of the TCC and providing the CCs with
all necessary documentation and information to facilitate their work. The Director would
also be the chief liaison person to the PCU.
(ii)    Oversee the work of the four technical advisors and other TCC staff and ensure that the
objectives and policies of the Project are understood and communicated to all
implementing agencies and personnel.
(iii)   Serve as secretary of the Project Policy Council and prepare, in consultation with his staff
and the CCs, agendas for Project Council meetings. Prepare minutes and monitor
decisions.
(iv)   Approve, in consultation with the respective technical advisor and the CCs, all terms of
reference for technical assistance and all specifications for goods financed under the
Project.
(v)    Oversee the preparation of and approve the Project Master Implementation Plan and
Component Detailed Implementation Plans. Ensure their efficient execution and periodic
updating.
(vi)   Authorize the PCU to prepare disbursement documentation and arrange for Ministerial
approval.
(vii)  Prepare periodic (quarterly) reports on Project implementation, based upon regular
reports provided by the implementing agencies and entities, forward the reports to the
Project Policy Council for discussion and approval, and transmit the approved reports to
the Bank and other donors participating in the Project.
(viii)  Organize monthly, or more frequent if necessary, meetings with all CCs and relevant
technical staff to discuss implementation issues. Ensure that implementing agencies or
entities receive the necessary support from the TCC and the PCU. Bring to the attention



212                             ANNEX 6
of the Project Policy Council and the Bank any issues that can not be resolved at the level
of the implementing agencies or entities.
(ix)   Serve as the main day-to-day liaison with the Bank in the management of the Project.
Specific Responsibilities of the Component Coordinators
11.   In addition to the general duties described above, the individuals assigned to their particular
component would have the following responsibilities:
12.   Primary Health Care:  The Component Coordinator for primary health care would have
responsibility for the following specific tasks:
(i)    Organize regular meetings with key counterparts of the PHC component, prepare
agendas, and write up and circulate Minutes of meetings.
(ii)    Monitor all aspects of the PHC component to ensure close cooperation among the WRH,
ARI/CDD and TB activities, cooperation with the rehabilitation of health facilities, and
(iii)   Prepare, in consultation with the WRH, ARI/CDD and TB counterparts, an annual
training plan for the component, including dates, destinations, purpose and participants
in foreign study tours, as well as planned in-country training. Monitor and report on the
number of workshops completed and number of participants trained. This should include
periodic surveys on the knowledge, attitudes, and clinical practices of health workers
trained under the Project.
(iv)   Coordinate all technical and logistical aspects of scheduled in-country training.
distribution and availability of PHC drugs provided under the Project.
(v)   In cooperation with the PCU, supervise the preparation for procurement of medical
equipment and supplies for the PHC facilities participating under the Project..
(vi)   Coordinate with other donors working on PHC activities, including attendance the
monthly UNDP donors meeting on health activities.
(vii)  Monitor on a regular basis the performance indicators established under the Project and
report progress and status quarterly.
13.   Facilities Management: The Component Coordinator for facilities management would have
responsibility for the following specific tasks:
(i)    Organize and chair meeting at least once every calendar month of the Ministry's
Buildings and Equipment Committee (BEC), including sending out typed agendas, writing
and circulating Minutes.
(ii)   In consultation with the BEC, and under the supervision of the Director of the TCC,
perform the tasks set out in the Program of Activities in the Civil Works Decision Book
(Chapter 7) including: drawing up Terms of Reference for the BEC members; delegating
tasks and responsibilities; drawing up detailed programs of work for every six month
period; supervising the appointment of consultant architects, engineers, equipment



213                               ANNEX 6
specialists; establishing contacts both within and outside the Ministry for dealing with
questions of clinical functions, i.e. quality, efficiency, nursing functions, technical
functions, specifications and space norms and standards, maintenance systems, staffing,
facility use, administrative questions, budgeting, procurement, etc.
(iii)   In consultation with the BEC and consultant architects/engineers, supervise the drawing
up of new norms and standards for health facilities to be approved by the Ministry;
finalize the list of facilities to be upgraded under the Project; establish a preliminary
works program and user groups at all institutions to be upgraded; provide quarterly
reports to the Director of the TCC on progress.
(iv)   In consultation with the BEC and the PCU, initiate surveys of the facilities to be
upgraded, using them to establish a schedule of works to be carried out; approve
proposals presented by the architect/engineer; authorize the preparation of contract
documents; and, assist in the implementation of tendering and awards.
(v)    During the rehabilitation work, monitor the supervision of the works by the consulting
architect/engineers, including countersigning certification to work completion and
acceptance by the Ministry; plan for and participate in accepting and commissioning the
completed facilities.
(vi)   In cooperation with the PCU, assist in preparing bidding documents for the procurement
of building equipment, medical equipment and supplies for the rehabilitated facilities, and
in the delivery and installation.
(vii)   Monitor on a regular basis the performance indicators established under the Project and
report progress and status quarterly.
(viii)  Use the Civil Works Decisions Book prepared under the Project as a reference book in
carrying out the above tasks.
(ix)   Prepare, in consultation with the BEC, an annual training plan for the component,
including dates, destinations, purpose and participants in foreign study tours, as well as
planned in-country training.
(x)    Coordinate all technical and logistical aspects of scheduled in-country training.
14.    Provider Payments:   The Component Coordinator for provider payments would have
responsibility for the following specific tasks:
(i)    Organize regular meetings with key counterparts of the Provider Payments component,
prepare agendas, and write up and circulate minutes of meetings.
(ii)    Monitor all aspects of the Provider Payments component to ensure close coordination
with the other components, and with the affected members of the medical community.
This would include evaluation of the Issyk-Kul provider payments program and
introduction of any lessons learned to the activities of the Project.
(iii)   Prepare an annual training plan for the component, including dates, destinations, purpose
and participants for planned in-country training as well as foreign study tours. Monitor



214                              ANNEX 6
and report on the number of workshops completed and number of participants trained.
This should include periodic surveys on the knowledge, attitudes, and clinical practices
of health workers trained under the Project.
(iv)   Coordinate all technical and logistical aspects of the major activities under the component.
(v)    In cooperation with the PCU, assist in the preparation of bidding documents for
procurement of medical equipment and supplies for the Family Practice Groups
participating under the Project, and supervise delivery and installation.
(vi)   Coordinate the identification and analysis of legislation or regulation impeding the
functioning of provider payment reforms and coordinate the preparation of
recommendations and proposed legislative and regulatory reforms.
(vii)   Monitor on a regular basis the performance indicators established under the Project and
report progress and status quarterly.
(viii)  Provide quarterly reports covering the Provider Payments component for inclusion in the
TCC quarterly report for the Project.
(ix)   Supervise implementation activities through regular field visits to Project activities.
15.   Pharmaceutical Management:  The Component Coordinator for pharmaceutical management
would have responsibility for the following specific tasks:
(i)    Assist the formation of, and participate in, the Ministry's Drug Working Group to
oversee procurement and distribution of Essential Drugs under the Project. The CC
would act as secretary and prepare periodic reports for the TCC on the Working Group's
activities and recommendations. This group would:
(a)    develop a formula for shipment of procured drugs among oblast Pharmacias and
Kyrgyz Pharmacia and develop rules of onward distribution.
(b)    participate in the elaboration of the list of 60 drugs for the first procurement and
determine relevant technical specifications to be included in International
Competitive Bidding documents;
(c)    develop labeling requirements for Essential Drugs procured under the Project and
determine relevant technical specifications to e included in ICB documents;
(d)   together with the Ministry of Finance, develop rules on the pricing of drugs
procured under the Project;
(e)   together with the Ministry of Finance, develop rules on taxation of the incomes
of oblast Pharmacias and Kyrgyz Pharmacia, with respect to their distribution of
drugs procured under the Project;
(f)    by means of regular report, audits and spot checks, monitor the distribution of
drugs procured under the Project.



215                              ANNEX 6
(ii)   Prepare, in consultation with the chief of the Drug Regulatory Organization (DRO), an
annual training plan for the DRO, including dates, destinations, purpose and participants
in foreign study tours, as well as planned in-country training.
(iii)   Coordinate all technical and logistical aspects of scheduled in-country training for
personnel of the DRO.
(iv)   Convene and chair an informal working group to design a monitoring system for the
Essential Drugs Program. Coordinate implementation of the monitoring program. This
program would include, among other things: ensure drug registration of the Essential
Drugs, quarterly surveys of a national sample of pharmacies to measure availability and
price of drugs, percentage of total prescriptions which are filled with Essential Drugs,
and percentage of drugs dispensed to "entitled" patients which consists of Essential
Drugs; annual surveys of physicians and pharmacists to measure awareness of and
support for the Essential Drugs Program; and, random checks of pharmacies to measure
quality of drugs offered for sale and extent to which pharnacies satisfy licensing
requirements.
(v)    Convene and chair a small working group to oversee production and distribution of the
Essential Drugs List. Specific responsibilities would include, among other things; the
writing of introduction and commentary; and the widest possible distribution of EDL
booklets, once these have been produced and delivered. Reconvene working group
approximately every two years, or otherwise as needed, in order to coordinate revision,
re-publication and distribution of a revised EDL.
(vi)   Participate, together with the Chief Therapist, other officials in the Ministry of Health,
professional medical workers, representatives from WHO and other international experts
in coordinated efforts to develop and implement new medical treatment guidelines
consistent with the Essential Drugs Program of the Kyrgyz Republic.
(vii)   Convene and chair an organizing committee each year to prepare an annual conference
on Drug Regulation Issues in the Kyrgyz Republic. The organizing committee would
include representative from the Ministry of health, the pharmaceutical industry, and
professional medical workers.
(viii)  Provide quarterly progress reports on the pharmaceutical component to be included in the
TCC quarterly progress report of Project activities.
(ix)   Provide appropriate supervision of pharmaceutical activities through field visits and
periodic trips to the various entities involved in implementing the component.

227                             ANNEX 8
KYRGYZ REPUBLIC
HEALTH SECTOR REFORM PROJECT
ANNEX 8. DESCRIPTIONS OF TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE
A. PRIMARY HEALTH CARE
A. 1: Women's Reproductive Health:
Consultants to Develop National Health and Sexually Transmitted Disease National Policy and Case
Management Guidelines.
Objective: Assist the MOH to develop a National Policy and Case management Guidelines based
upon WHO's "Mother-Baby Packages", and for Sexually Transmitted Diseases. This would include the
translation of WHO materials into Russian, review and revise the materials with a committee of national
experts to develop national guidelines for four levels of health facilities: i) Specialist tertiary and Oblast
hospitals; ii) central raion hospitals; iii) polyclinics, SVAa and APTKs; and iv) feldsher accoucheur posts.
Duration: Two person months of services in year one (February, 1996), and one person month
of services the next three years for a total of five person months. It is expected that the Government will
contract directly with WHO for the provision of a team of experts with previous experience working on
health problems in the former Soviet Union. The team should include specialists in obstetrics,
neonatology and venerology.
Outcome: National Guidelines
A.2: ARI/CDD:
Consultants to Develop National Health Policy in Acute Respiritory and infectious Diseases, and
Communicable and Diahhreal Diseases:
Objective: To train hospital specialists to develop "Model Training Units" in childhood acute
respiratory diseases and diarrheal diseases, develop a "Mini-Family Doctor Training Course" and training
trainers for SVA, FAP and polyclinic staff, and assist the MOH to establish a data base for case
management protocols and rational drug prescribing. The consultants will work with local expert
conmmittees, appointed by the MOH, in the review and local adaptation of WHO and other internationally
recognized standard clinical guidelines related to the treatment of common childhood illnesses. The
expert Committees will develop National Case Management Guidelines to be entered into a computer
database in the MOH's Department of Treatment and Prevention and to serve as training materials for
a series of workshops for clinical personnel at four levels of health facilities: i) Specialist tertiary and
Oblast hospitals; ii) central raion hospitals; iii) polyclinics, SVAa and APTKs; and iv) feldsher
accoucheur posts..
Duration: Two person months of services in year one (February, 1996), one person month of
services the next year and one half person month the following two yeafs for a total of four person
months. It is expected that the Government will contract directly with WHO for the provision of a teamn
of experts with previous experience working on health problems in the former Soviet Union. The team
should include specialists in pediatricians and infectionists.
Outcome: National Guidelines and Training Course Materials



228                            ANNEX 8
A.3: TB:
(NOTE: This technical assistance will be contracted directly with WHO given the exclusive use of WHO
methodology and experience)
Consultants for National Training Course (2, twice at the beginning of Year 1 and 2)
Objective: To assist national trainers coordinate a training course on WHO tuberculosis control
strategy, for national level officers, and up-date national level staff on modem practices in tuberculosis
control.
Duration: 7 day each
Outcome: Trained national officers who will train lower level officers.
Consultant for Laboratory Course (1, Twice at the beginning of year I and 3)
Objective: To formally train national and oblast level microbiologists on adequate practices in
smear microscopy.
Duration: 15 days, year one - 7 days, year 2.
Outcome: Fully trained national and oblast laboratory heads who will be capable to train lower
level staff.
External Consultant for Monitoring Process
Objective: To assist WHO staff in monitoring progress of implementation of the National
Tuberculosis Program and to review results achieved, identify and address problems encountered during
programn implementation together with a local team from the National Tuberculosis Institute, and prepare
a report on progress of the project for use by the MOH, WHO and the World Bank.
Duration: I mission at month 6 after the start of the project, then 2 missions every year of 2
weeks each.
Outcome: Reports on the status of project implementation for use by the Policy Council and
donors.
B. FACILITIES MANAGEMENT
Consultant in Estate Management and Facility Rehabilitation
Objective: To establish new procedures for health facility management.
Duration: One person month in year 1, and one person month in year 2, for a total of 2 person
months.
Outcome: New procedures



229                            ANNEX 8
Consultants in Architectural/ Engineering Services (Local)
Objective: To develop and design rehabilitation specifications and oversee implementation to
ensure quality control.
Duration: To be implemented in the first two years of the project.
Outcome: 30 rehabilitated medical facilities.
C. MEDICAL CARE PROVIDER PAYMENTS
Consultants for Medical Care Provider Payment activities in establishing Family Group Practices and
enrollment of patients, creating a an incentive-based payment system for medical providers, developing
an MIS and Management Capacity, instituting quality assurance measures, and training of family doctors.
The international technical assistance (approximately 30 person months) will work closely with a broad
array of local consultants (approximately 384 Person Years). The management approach would be to
have an international consulting firm provide the international technical assistance services, and local
consultants, hired as individuals, provide the specialized tasks identified. The breakdown is as follows:
A. Family Practice Groups International Consultants to Develop Financial and Clinical Infornation
Systems (4 Person Months) and Marketing (1 PM) for a total of 5 PM. Local consultants to provide
computer systems advice (8 Person Years), one Practice Manager for every five FPG for a total of 200
Person Years, two fundholding specialists (8 Person Years), and secretary (4 Person years).
Objective: To establish 300 family practice groups and enroll 4000 patients in each.
Duration: To be implemented over a four year period.
Outcome: Established family practice groups and a Primary Care Physicians Association.
B. International Consultants to create an incentive-based payment system for medical providers by
establishment of a Health Fund. Program Design consultants (8 Person Months), Fund /Banking/Auditing
specialist (2.5 PM), Fundholding specialist (3 PM), and hospital payments specialist (3 PM) for a total
of 12.5 PM. Four local consultants for computer specialists for the Fund (16 Person Years) and four
computer consultants (12 person years).
Objective: To create an incentive-based payment system for medical providers and establish a
medical fund for centralizing payments to providers.
Dureation: To be implemented over a four year period.
Outcome:   A medical fund making payments to medical providers under an incentive-based
system.
C. International Consultants to develop a Management Information System and management capacity by
establishing a Hospital Association and establishing a training capacity in a management institute. cost
accounting and clinical information systems consultant (3 PM), and a management consultant (2PM)
would be provided. Local consultants in hospital payments ( 2 for 8 Person Years), cost accounting (2



230                             ANNEX 8
for 8 Person Years), clinical information systems (2 for 8 Person Years), management (2 for 8 Person
Years), computer specialist (2 for 8 Person Years), and a secretary (4 Person Years).
Objective: To establish a Hospital Association and develop a management information system
and training capacity.
Outcome: A hospital association capable of representing and training hospital administrators in
managing new provider payment systems.
D. International Consultants to develop a quality assurance institution - Accreditation Commission - to
license and accredit physicians and FPGs to practice and ensure quality control. Consultants in
accreditation (1 Person Month) and quality improvement (3 Person Months) would be provided. Local
consultants in quality improvement (4 for 16 Person Years), accreditation (2 for 8 Person Years),
accreditation surveys (4 for 16 Person years), computer specialist (2 for 8 Person Years), and a secretary
(4 Person Years) would be provided.
Objective: To develop quality assurance through an Accreditation Conmiission and ensure quality
through inspections and self-regulation.
Duration: To be implemented over four years.
Outcome: A functioning Accreditation Commission capable of assuring quality control.
E. International Consultants to establish a training programn for family doctors. Consultants in medical
training (3 Person Months) and the use of an NGO to provide resident training personnel in primary care
would be provided. Local consultants in clinical training (10 for 40 Person Years) would be provided.
Objective: To establish a training capacity to train 1200 primary care physicians in famfly
practice medicine.
Duration: To be implemented over four years.
Outcome: 1200 trained family doctors.

243                             ANNEX 11
KYRGYZ REPUBLIC
HEALTH SECTOR REFORM PROJECT
ANNEX 11: IMPLEMENTATION ACTIONS, REPORTING AND MONITORING
A. Implementation Actions and Progress Reports Required by the Government
1.    Specific measures need to be taken during implementation of the project to support the project's
objectives and the wider objectives of the Borrower, as set forth in its policy statement. To this end, the
Borrower and the Association have agreed on a series of actions in connection with the monitoring of the
implementation of the project (the action plan) within the framework a schedule of regular monitoring
and reporting.
2.    During the execution of the project, the Borrower, through the TCC, will furnish to the
Association regular annual progress reports and action plans. These reports and plans should be
supplemented by shorter, quarterly reports. The annual and quarterly reports and plans should cover:
(a)    project implementation progress;
(b)   the level of funding of the health sector;
(c)   fulfillment of conditions in the Development Credit Agreement;
(d)    procurement activities, expenditures and disbursements in a format as set forth in para.
4.26;
(e)    details on management and operations of the project, including performance of the PCU
and the TCC, and of consultants hired under the project.
3.    The part of the reports and plans dealing with the action plan set forth in paragraphs 4-8 below
should review progress made to date in the period covered by the report, and actions to be taken in the
following period. Reports should address both the actions to be taken by the Borrower, as listed below,
and the Performance Monitoring Indicators.
4.    By December 31, 1996, The Borrower, through its Ministry of Health, will:
(a)    Present to the Association for review and comments its MANAS Health Care Reform
Program and a schedule of rationalization of health facilities and thereafter carry out the
program in accordance with that schedule, taking into account the comments of the
Association (para. 1.49);
(b)    Combine services in the health facilities selected as Oblast Model Polyclinics where
training under the PHC component will be carried out, so that services for pediatrics,
women's health and general adult health will be offered in one building (para. 3.19).
(c)    Ensure timely supply and regular replenishment to all facilities where training under the
PHC component is carried out of project financed equipment, drugs and other materials,
and ensure that part of these drugs are provided free of charge to personnel of FAPs and
ambulatory centers participating in the training programs as trainees (para. 3.19);
(d)    Establish new national case management guidelines, treatment protocols and enabling
legislation (para. 3.9, 3.13, 3.25, 3.28, 3.62);
(e)   Issue guidelines, acceptable to the Association, to health authorities at all levels on
leasing of publicly owned health premises to family group practices (para. 3.64 (a));
(f)    Carry out a study of the levels of patients' referrals from primary care physicians to
specialists and for diagnostic tests in Bishkek City and Chui Oblasts. Not later than June



244                              ANNEX 11
30, 1997 it will submit this study to the Association for review and comments, and it will
subsequently implement the agreed recommendations (para. 3.64 (b));
(g)    Appoint a standing committee for the Essential Drugs Programn, consistent with authority
provided by the "Law on Medicines" and as provided by the rules adopted on compiling
and maintaining its EDL (para. 3.78).
5.     By June 30, 1997 and thereafter at the end of each annual drug procurement cycle, the
Borrower's MOH will review drug procurement and distribution so as to assure that privately owned drug
wholesalers and retailers are not disadvantaged compared to remaining state-owned companies (para.
3.80).
6.     By December 31, 1997, the Borrower, through its Ministry of Health, will:
(a)    Design and implement a national health accounts system to be able to track allocation of
resources for health and the flow of funds in the health sector (para. 3.64 (c));
(b)    Establish a data base of National Case Management Guidelines for women's reproductive
health, STDs, ARI/CDD and TB, based on the WHO recommended guidelines, together
with treatmnent protocols for all those conditions, indicating that drugs used should be
from its Essential Drug List only, and thereafter update and distribute these protocols
regularly to health workers nationwide (para. 3.23);
(c)    (i) establish and thereafter maintain a Health Fund into which national, oblast, municipal
and raion level health authorities will contribute and out of which medical providers will
be paid; (ii) issue guidelines on the manner and level of contribution by these health
authorities and the characteristics and costs of the services to be purchased; and, (iii)
pass legislation allowing establishment of primary health care provider groups as non-
profit entities and opening of bank accounts by such groups (para. 3.64 (c));
7.     By January 31, 1998 and thereafter, the Borrower will allocate budget resources for procurement
and reimbursement of pharmaceuticals solely to pharmaceuticals listed on its Essential Drug List and
registered in the country (para. 3.77);
8.    In each medical facility to be renovated under the project the Borrower, through its MOH, will
establish a stakeholder group consisting of health authorities and local government officials, before
renovation is undertaken (para. 3.36 and Annex 3).
B. Performance Monitoring Indicators
9.    In addition to the reporting requirements listed above the TCC will be required to monitor the
performance indicators. These indicators are broken into three types for each component: input, output
and impact. Input indicators are activities which are aimed to improve parameters which have a direct
impact on the health status, not do not themselves directly affect the health status, such as training.
Output indicators monitor the impact of input indicators and include parameters which are expected to
influence the health status directly such as number of patients being treated with new protocols. Impact
indicators monitor the degree to which project related changes in input and output parameters will result
in improvement of the health status, such as the improvement in the maternal mortality rate. Following
is a list of indicators identified for each component and targets that are to be achieved through the project.

259                            ANNEX 14
KYRGYZ REPUBLIC
HEALTH SECTOR REFORM PROJECT
ANNEX 14: OTHER DONOR ACTIVITIES AND COORDINATION
1.    Summary of donor activities in the Kyrgz Republic: The major donor organizations working
in the Kyrgyz Republic's health sector are USAID, UNICEF, WHO, and UNDP. USAID, UNICEF and
UNDP all have small country offices in Bishkek. USAID has a regional office in Almaty and the
UNICEF country office is supervised by the Area Office for Central Asian, located in Islaniabad,
Pakistan. UNFPA plans to set up a regional office with a regional advisor. GTZ, the German
government's technical assistance agency, and DANIDA, the Danish government's development agency
also have small offices with a resident country program officer. Several other agencies are working on
emergency food programs (Red Cross, Mercy Corps International, France Liberte, etc.).
2.    Summary of organizations involved in health reform activities: WHO/EURO, UNDP and
TICA, the Turkish development agency are supporting the MANAS Health Care Reform Project. This
project is due to finish in September 1995. The MANAS project has developed a framework for health
planning and strengthened the management capacity of selected MOH staff. USAID is funding health
fuiance reform through the Abt Associates demonstration site in Issyk Kul. ODA have funded study tours
for key central and oblast health administrators to look at health reform in the U.K. and Scandinavia. In
early 1996, GTZ will appoint a long term health policy advisor to the President and MOH, with
particular emphasis on health education , health insurance and drug regulation.
3.    Summary of organizations involved in essential drugs programs: WHO are providing technical
assistance for the development of a national essential drugs and rational prescribing program. ODA, the
British development agency provided $400,000 to DAP/EURO/WHO for this program. GTZ plans to
bring in short term advisors to work on establishing a drug's regulation and licensing body for the Kyrgyz
Republic. UNDP is administering the purchase of $1.2 million of emergency drugs in 1995, with money
donated by DANIDA.
4.    Summary of organizations involved in children's health activities:
(a)    Expanded Program of Immunization: UNICEF is providing primary series vaccines and
supplies using a Japanese government grant. UNICEF is also providing technical
assistance and has advocated for reducing the list of contraindications observed. USAID
has donated emergency vaccines and provided technical assistance and strengthening of
cold chain through the "Basics Project".
(b)    Acute Respiratory Infections and Control of Diarrheal Diseases: UNICEF has donated
emergency drugs for winter and summer programs and funded training of health workers
at the central, oblast, and peripheral levels. Case management guidelines and health
education materials have also been provided.
(c)    Breastfeeding: UNICEF and USAID (through the Wellstart project) have supported some
training of health workers. UNICEF has worked closely with the MOH to rewrite
"Decree #55" which outlines birth house operations. The rewritten decree promotes baby
friendly practices and emphasizes breastfeeding. It is now in the approval process of the
MOH and should be adopted by the end of 1995.



260                            ANNEX 14
(d)   Iodine Deficiency Disease: UNICEF is assisting the government develop a national plan
for iodized salt. Legislation has now been passed which requires that only iodized salt
is imported into the Republic. The GOK has set the goal of making iodized salt available
for human consumption throughout the Republic by the end of 1995.
5.    A summary of agencies involved in women's reproductive health activities: USAID and
UNFPA are the lead agencies working on these activities. USAID, working through a number of
contractors (Futures Group, SOMARC, JHIEPGO, AVSC, PCS) is providing technical assistance to
government policy makers and health workers and creating a market for contraceptives through social
marketing. UNFPA is supplying contraceptives and has begun developing an STD/FP health education
program for Bishkek. Under contract with UNFPA, Family Health International is developing a pilot
project which trains midwives to insert IUDs. The WHO Regional AIDS Control Office in Almaty is
funding an sexually transmitted diseases expert to conduct a regional workshop on STD management in
Tashkent. Key health personnel from the Kyrgyz Republic will attend this workshop.
6.    Food and Clothing Assistance: Several donor organizations are active in providing food
assistance to the country. Primary donors include: France Liberte; the European Union; Red
Barnett/Save the Children, Denmark; The International Federation of the Red Cross and Red Crescent
Societies; UNICEF; Mercy Corps International; and German Agro Action.
7.    Planned assistance for the Fall of 1995 includes: German Agro Action supplying 2,000 tons of
wheat flour, 200 tons of sunflower oil for distribution to the poor, the elderly, the disabled, and orphans
in Djalal-Abad and Osh Oblasts; France Liberte will supply: 4,200 tons of Flour, sugar, oil, salt for
150,000 persons (10,000 prisoners) in Talas, Naryn, Issyk-Kul, Chui Oblasts. Mercy Corps International
will distribute 1,500 metric tons of Rice and 800 metric tons of vegetable oil to institutions throughout
the Republic in coordination with the Ministries of Health, Education, and Social Protection and be
distributed primarily to schools, and maternity houses. UNICEF will continue to supply high protein
food in the form of BP-5 biscuits and will distribute through schools and peripheral level health facilities.
8.    Planned assistance for clothing this fall will include UNICEF's distribution of $100,000 worth
of winter coats and shoes for children 3 - 11 years old. France Liberte will also distribute clothing this
fall and will also provide hygienic products and bed linens (140 tons) to 40,000 persons in 45 institutions
and 75 hospitals in Osh and Djalal-Abad Oblasts.
9.    Coordination of Other Donor Activities with the Proposed World Bank Reform Project:
(a)    The pharmaceutical management component of the World Bank project will work closely
with DPA/WHO/EURO and GTZ on the implementation of an essential drugs program.
Meetings between these various agencies are ongoing and the coordination is good.
(b)    The health finance component of the World Bank project will have to compliment the
ongoing USAID funded activities through the Abt Associates demonstration project in
Issyk Kul.
(c)    A member of Abt Associates acted as an observer on the March 1995 World Bank
Mission, thereby facilitating close coordination between the USAID and World Bank
activities.
(d)    The primary health care component of the World Bank project has been developed to
compliment the activities of UNICEF, USAID and WHO. The ARI/CDD sub-component



261                             ANNEX 14
will provide technical assistance and the long term supply of essential drugs to support
UNICEF's ARI and CDD programs. The Tuberculosis sub-component will support the
ongoing technical assistance provided by WHO. The Women's Reproductive Health sub-
component will compliment the family planning activities of USAID and UNFPA by
focusing on obstetric care, perinatal care and the treatment of sexually transmitted
diseases.
